## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of a chemical species concentration as a function of its current concentration and time. The core relationship is the rate law dA/dt = f(A), potentially with explicit time dependence for non-autonomous or complex reaction systems.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to concentration squared)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate law)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (combination of first and second order)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (saturation kinetics)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse reaction with equilibrium)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalysis)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (substrate inhibition)
- Time-modulated decay: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-dependent rate coefficient)
- Fractional order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (generalized rate with constant source/sink)
- Competitive pathway: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) + c2 * A (parallel Michaelis-Menten and first-order)
- Power-law with time dependence: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * t**c2 (dispersive kinetics in heterogeneous media)
- Sigmoidal rate: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (Hill-type cooperative kinetics)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Pure concentration dependence (no explicit t) → elementary reaction rate law dA/dt = k*A^n, suggesting a well-mixed homogeneous reaction
- Linear dependence on A → first-order kinetics, characteristic of radioactive decay, unimolecular decomposition, or pseudo-first-order conditions
- Quadratic dependence on A → second-order kinetics from bimolecular collisions (2A → products)
- Rational function of A (numerator/denominator both involving A) → enzyme kinetics or surface-catalyzed reactions with adsorption-desorption equilibria
- Product form A*(c-A) → autocatalytic or logistic growth where the product catalyzes its own formation from a finite substrate pool
- Explicit time dependence in rate constant → photochemical reactions, temperature ramps, or heterogeneous/fractal kinetics with time-dependent diffusion
- Non-integer power of A → fractal reaction kinetics or effective rate laws from underlying complex mechanisms
- Constant additive term independent of A → zero-order production or continuous external feed into the reactor
- Negative square root or fractional power of A → diffusion-limited surface reactions or half-order kinetics in catalysis
- Sum of multiple power-law terms in A → parallel competing reaction pathways each with different molecularity
